dir=\"auto\"\u003e{:toc}\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003edummy item\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIn this section, we will take a deep dive into typing and type checking. You should hopefully get a much better idea of the implications of a type system.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBefore proceeding, it's worth asking if are types even necessary to create a programming language?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eYes! It is possible to have a language with no types. Assembly languages are one such example of languages with no type system. They just have a register that holds a 32 (or 64) bit value. The value could represent anything (an integer, float, pointer, etc.). \u003ca href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BLISS\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003eBLISS\u003c/a\u003e is another example of a language with no types.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"MODULE E1 (MAIN = CTRL) =\nBEGIN\nFORWARD ROUTINE\n    CTRL,\n    STEP;\nROUTINE CTRL =\nBEGIN\n    EXTERNAL ROUTINE\n        GETNUM,     ! Input a number from terminal\n        PUTNUM;     ! Output a number to terminal\n    LOCAL\n        X,          ! Storage for input value\n        Y;          ! Storage for output value\n    GETNUM(X);\n    Y = STEP(.X);\n    PUTNUM(.Y)\n    END;\nROUTINE STEP(A) =\n    (.A+1);\nEND\nELUDOM\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eMODULE E1 (MAIN = CTRL) =\nBEGIN\nFORWARD ROUTINE\n    CTRL,\n    STEP;\nROUTINE CTRL =\nBEGIN\n    EXTERNAL ROUTINE\n        GETNUM,     ! Input a number from terminal\n        PUTNUM;     ! Output a number to terminal\n    LOCAL\n        X,          ! Storage for input value\n        Y;          ! Storage for output value\n    GETNUM(X);\n    Y = STEP(.X);\n    PUTNUM(.Y)\n    END;\nROUTINE STEP(A) =\n    (.A+1);\nEND\nELUDOM\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBut virtually all modern languages have a type system, since it makes programming so much easier and safer.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMust every variable have a type in a typed language?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eNo! In Python for example, variables are not associated with types.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"# Python\ndef foo(q):\n  if q:\n    x = \u0026quot;What's my type?\u0026quot; # string\n  ...\n  x = 10 # int\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e# Python\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003edef\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003efoo\u003c/span\u003e(\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eq\u003c/span\u003e):\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eif\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eq\u003c/span\u003e:\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003ex\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\"What's my type?\"\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e# string\u003c/span\u003e\n  ...\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003ex\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e10\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e# int\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIn general, many dynamically typed (don't worry, we will cover them in this lecture) languages don't associate variables with types. However, note that a value is \u003cstrong\u003ealways\u003c/strong\u003e associated with a type.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eTypes can broadly be classified into two categories, primitive and composite. Primitive data types are a set of types from which other types are constructed. Composite data types are those types which can be constructed using primitive and composite data types.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eExamples of primitive data types:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eIntegers\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eBooleans\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eCharacters\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eEnumerated types (Enums)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eFloats\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ePointers\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eExamples of derived data types:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eArrays\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eStructs\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eVariants/Unions\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eObjects\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eTuples\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eContainers\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThere can also be data types that don't fall into either category.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eFunctions\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eGeneric types\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eBoxed types\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e{: .note}\nA boxed type is just an object whose only data member is a \u003cem\u003eprimitive\u003c/em\u003e (like an \u003ccode\u003eint\u003c/code\u003e or a \u003ccode\u003efloat\u003c/code\u003e)\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"class Integer {\n public:\n   int get() const { return val_; }\n private:\n   int val_;\n};\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eclass\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003eInteger\u003c/span\u003e {\n \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003epublic:\u003c/span\u003e\n   \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eint\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003eget\u003c/span\u003e() \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003econst\u003c/span\u003e { \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003ereturn\u003c/span\u003e val_; }\n \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eprivate:\u003c/span\u003e\n   \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eint\u003c/span\u003e val_;\n};\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIn languages like Python that pass by object reference, this lets you \"change\" a primitive type's value!\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eType checking\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-type-checking\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Type checking\" href=\"#type-checking\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eType checking is the process of verifying and enforcing constriants on types. Type checking can occur during compile time (static) or during run time (dynamic). The language can also specify the degree of strictness for type checking (strong and weak type checking). We will go into more detail on all of these topics.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cmarkdown-accessiblity-table\u003e\u003ctable\u003e\n\u003cthead\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003cth align=\"center\"\u003e\u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"/UCLA-CS-131/fall-23-website/blob/main/lectures/%7B%7Bsite.baseurl%7D%7D/assets/lecture-notes/07/type-checking-approaches.png\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"/UCLA-CS-131/fall-23-website/raw/main/lectures/%7B%7Bsite.baseurl%7D%7D/assets/lecture-notes/07/type-checking-approaches.png\" alt=\"type-checking\" style=\"max-width: 100%;\"\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/th\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003c/thead\u003e\n\u003ctbody\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd align=\"center\"\u003eType checking approaches. Type checkers can be classified on the basis of whether they run during compile time or during run time. Type checkers can also be classified on the basis of strictness (strong or weak).\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003c/tbody\u003e\n\u003c/table\u003e\u003c/markdown-accessiblity-table\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eStatic typing\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-static-typing\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Static typing\" href=\"#static-typing\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eStatic typing is the process of verifying that all operations in a program are consistent with the types of the operands prior to program execution. Types can either be explicitly specified (like in C++) or can be inferred from code (like in Haskell). For inferred types, if the type checker cannot assign distinct types to all variables, functions, and expressions or cannot verify type safety, then it generates an error.\nBut if a program type checks, then it means the code is (largely) type safe, and few if any run time checks need to be performed.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e{: .note }\nTo support static typing, a language \u003cstrong\u003emust have\u003c/strong\u003e a fixed type bound to each variable at the time of definition.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch4 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eType Inference\u003c/h4\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-type-inference\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Type Inference\" href=\"#type-inference\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eType inference refers to the automatic detection of types of expressions or variables in a language. Consider the following example:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"void foo(_____ x, _____ y) {\n  cout \u0026lt;\u0026lt; x + 10;\n  cout \u0026lt;\u0026lt; y + \u0026quot; is a string!\u0026quot;;\n}\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003evoid\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003efoo\u003c/span\u003e(_____ x, _____ y) {\n  cout \u0026lt;\u0026lt; x + \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e10\u003c/span\u003e;\n  cout \u0026lt;\u0026lt; y + \u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003e is a string!\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/span\u003e;\n}\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhat would be the types of \u003ccode\u003ex\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003ey\u003c/code\u003e? \u003ccode\u003eint\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003estring\u003c/code\u003e, right! The compiler can infer that \u003ccode\u003ey\u003c/code\u003e is an \u003ccode\u003estring\u003c/code\u003e from the fact that we perform the operation \u003ccode\u003ey + \" is a string\"\u003c/code\u003e, which is only valid if \u003ccode\u003ey\u003c/code\u003e is a \u003ccode\u003estring\u003c/code\u003e. What about \u003ccode\u003ex\u003c/code\u003e? It seems like \u003ccode\u003ex\u003c/code\u003e can only be an \u003ccode\u003eint\u003c/code\u003e. But consider this example:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"void foo(_____ x, _____ y) {\n  cout \u0026lt;\u0026lt; x + 10;\n  cout \u0026lt;\u0026lt; y + \u0026quot; is a string!\u0026quot;;\n}\nvoid bar() {\n  double d = 3.14;\n  foo(d,\u0026quot;barf\u0026quot;);\n}\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003evoid\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003efoo\u003c/span\u003e(_____ x, _____ y) {\n  cout \u0026lt;\u0026lt; x + \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e10\u003c/span\u003e;\n  cout \u0026lt;\u0026lt; y + \u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003e is a string!\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/span\u003e;\n}\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003evoid\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003ebar\u003c/span\u003e() {\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003edouble\u003c/span\u003e d = \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e3.14\u003c/span\u003e;\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003efoo\u003c/span\u003e(d,\u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003ebarf\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/span\u003e);\n}\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eHere, it makes more sense for \u003ccode\u003ex\u003c/code\u003e to be a \u003ccode\u003edouble\u003c/code\u003e. So type inference is actually a complex constraint satisfaction problem.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e{: .note }\nA fun observation from Matt - because C and C++ allow pointer arithmetic, in theory \u003ccode\u003ex\u003c/code\u003e could also be a pointer. Wonky!\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMany statically typed languages now offer some form of type inference. C++ has the \u003ccode\u003eauto\u003c/code\u003e keyword:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"// C++ type inference with auto\nint main() {\n  auto x = 3.14159; // x is of type int\n  vector\u0026lt;int\u0026gt; v;\n  ...\n\n  for (auto item: v) { // item is of type int\n    cout \u0026lt;\u0026lt; item \u0026lt;\u0026lt; endl;\n  }\n\n  auto it = v.begin(); // it is of type vector\u0026lt;int\u0026gt;::iterator\n  while(it != v.end()) {\n    cout \u0026lt;\u0026lt; *it \u0026lt;\u0026lt; endl;\n    ++it;\n  }\n}\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e C++ type inference with auto\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eint\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003emain\u003c/span\u003e() {\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eauto\u003c/span\u003e x = \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e3.14159\u003c/span\u003e; \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e x is of type int\u003c/span\u003e\n  vector\u0026lt;\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eint\u003c/span\u003e\u0026gt; v;\n  ...\n\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003efor\u003c/span\u003e (\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eauto\u003c/span\u003e item: v) { \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e item is of type int\u003c/span\u003e\n    cout \u0026lt;\u0026lt; item \u0026lt;\u0026lt; endl;\n  }\n\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eauto\u003c/span\u003e it = v.\u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003ebegin\u003c/span\u003e(); \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e it is of type vector\u0026lt;int\u0026gt;::iterator\u003c/span\u003e\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003ewhile\u003c/span\u003e(it != v.\u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003eend\u003c/span\u003e()) {\n    cout \u0026lt;\u0026lt; *it \u0026lt;\u0026lt; endl;\n    ++it;\n  }\n}\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e{: .note }\nType inference has limitations! Most languages (like C++, Java, or Rust) will struggle with generic types and iterators; you'll be forced to write type annotations in some areas.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eGo similarly infers the type of variables from the right-hand-side expression\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-go notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"// GoLang type inference\nfunc main() {\n  msg := \u0026quot;I like languages\u0026quot;; // string\n  n := 5 // int\n  for i := n; i \u0026gt; 0; i-- {\n    fmt.Println(msg);\n  }\n}\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// GoLang type inference\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003efunc\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003emain\u003c/span\u003e() {\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003emsg\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e:=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\"I like languages\"\u003c/span\u003e; \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// string\u003c/span\u003e\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003en\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e:=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e5\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// int\u003c/span\u003e\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003efor\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003ei\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e:=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003en\u003c/span\u003e; \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003ei\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e\u0026gt;\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e0\u003c/span\u003e; \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003ei\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e--\u003c/span\u003e {\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003efmt\u003c/span\u003e.\u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003ePrintln\u003c/span\u003e(\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003emsg\u003c/span\u003e);\n  }\n}\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch4 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eConservatism\u003c/h4\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-conservatism\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Conservatism\" href=\"#conservatism\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eStatic type checking is inherently conservative. This means that the static type checker will disallow perfectly valid programs that never violate typing rules.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e{: .note }\nThis is due to the fact that for Turing-complete languages, it is not possible to have a \u003cem\u003esound\u003c/em\u003e (meaning all incorrect programs are rejected), \u003cem\u003edecidable\u003c/em\u003e (meaning that it is possible to write an algorithm that determines whether a program is well-typed), and \u003cem\u003ecomplete\u003c/em\u003e (meaning no correct programs are rejected) type system. This follows from \u003ca href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/G%C3%B6del%27s_incompleteness_theorems\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003eG枚del's incompleteness theorems\u003c/a\u003e. (Don't worry if you don't understand this, it won't be on the exam :))\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eFor an example, consider the following program:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"class Mammal {\npublic:\n virtual void makeNoise() { cout \u0026lt;\u0026lt; \u0026quot;Breathe\\n\u0026quot;; }\n};\nclass Dog: public Mammal {\npublic:\n void makeNoise() override { cout \u0026lt;\u0026lt; \u0026quot;Ruff\\n\u0026quot;; }\n void bite() { cout \u0026lt;\u0026lt; \u0026quot;Chomp\\n\u0026quot;; }\n};\nclass Cat: public Mammal {\npublic:\n void makeNoise() override { cout \u0026lt;\u0026lt; \u0026quot;Meow!\\n\u0026quot;; }\n void scratch() { cout \u0026lt;\u0026lt; \u0026quot;Scrape!\\n\u0026quot;; }\n};\n\nvoid handlePet(Mammal\u0026amp; m, bool bite, bool scratch) {\n m.makeNoise();\n if (bite)\n   m.bite();\n if (scratch)\n   m.scratch();\n}\n\nint main() {\n Dog spot;\n Cat meowmer;\n handlePet(spot, true, false);\n handlePet(meowmer, false, true);\n}\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003eBreathe\u003cspan class=\"pl-cce\"\u003e\\n\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/span\u003e; }\n};\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eclass\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003eDog\u003c/span\u003e: \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003epublic\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003eMammal\u003c/span\u003e {\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003epublic:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003evoid\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003emakeNoise\u003c/span\u003e() \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eoverride\u003c/span\u003e { cout \u0026lt;\u0026lt; \u003cspan }\n \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003evoid\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003ebite\u003c/span\u003e() { cout \u0026lt;\u0026lt; \u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eclass\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003eCat\u003c/span\u003e: \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003epublic\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003ebite\u003c/span\u003e();\n \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eif\u003c/span\u003e (scratch)\n   m.\u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003escratch\u003c/span\u003e();\n}\n\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eint\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003emain\u003c/span\u003e() {\n Dog spot;\n Cat meowmer;\n \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003ehandlePet\u003c/span\u003e(spot, \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003etrue\u003c/span\u003e, \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003efalse\u003c/span\u003e);\n \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003ehandlePet\u003c/span\u003e(meowmer, \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003efalse\u003c/span\u003e, \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003etrue\u003c/span\u003e);\n}\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe compiler generates an error during the compilation of this code\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-text-shell-session notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"error: no member named 'scratch' in 'Mammal'\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003eerror: no member named 'scratch' in 'Mammal'\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eeven though the code only asks \u003ccode\u003eDog\u003c/code\u003es to \u003ccode\u003ebite\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003eCat\u003c/code\u003es to \u003ccode\u003escratch\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003ePros of static type checking\u003c/strong\u003e:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eProduces faster code (since we don't have to type check during run time)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eAllows for earlier bug detection (at compile time)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eNo need to write custom type checks\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eCons of static type checking\u003c/strong\u003e:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eStatic typing is conservative and may error our perfectly valid code\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eIt requires a type checking phase before execution, which can be slow\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eDynamic type checking is the process of verifying the type safety of a program at run time. If the code is attempting an illegal operation on a variable's value, an exception is generated and the program crashes. Here are some examples of dynamic type checking at run time.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"def add(x,y):\n print(x + y)\n\ndef foo():\n a = 10\n b = \u0026quot;cooties\u0026quot;\n add(a,b)\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eHow does a program written in a dynamically typed language detect type violations?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWell, in dynamically typed languages, \u003cstrong\u003etypes are associated with values -- not variables\u003c/strong\u003e! In other words, variables do not have types in dynamically typed languages.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eUsually the compiler/interpreter would use a \u003cem\u003etype tag\u003c/em\u003e, an extra piece of data stored along with each value that indicates the type of the value.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"def add(x,y):\n print(x + y)\n\ndef foo():\n a = 10\n b = \u0026quot;cooties\u0026quot;\n add(a, b)\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003edef\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003eadd\u003c/span\u003e(\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003ex\u003c/span\u003e,\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003ey\u003c/span\u003e):\n \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003eprint\u003c/span\u003e(\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003ex\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e+\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\"cooties\"\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003eadd\u003c/span\u003e(\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003ea\u003c/span\u003e, \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eb\u003c/span\u003e)\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eSo in this example, the compiler would store the fact that the value \u003ccode\u003ea\u003c/code\u003e is pointing to is an \u003ccode\u003eint\u003c/code\u003e with value \u003ccode\u003e10\u003c/code\u003e, and \u003ccode\u003eb\u003c/code\u003e is a \u003ccode\u003estring\u003c/code\u003e with value \u003ccode\u003ecooties\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eSometimes statically typed languages also need to perform run time type checks. This is most often seen during down-casting (when casting an object from a child class to a parent class). Consider the following example.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"class nullptr)\n    s-\u0026gt;getDrunkAtParty();\n}\nint main() {\n  Doctor *d = new Doctor(\u0026quot;Dr. Fauci\u0026quot;);\n  partay(d);\n  delete d;\n}\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eclass\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003ePerson\u003c/span\u003e { ... };\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eclass\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003epartay\u003c/span\u003e(d);\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003edelete\u003c/span\u003e d;\n}\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003edynamic_cast\u003c/code\u003e does a run time check to ensure that the type conversion (from \u003ccode\u003ePerson*\u003c/code\u003e to \u003ccode\u003eStudent*\u003c/code\u003e) we are performing is valid. If it isn't valid, \u003ccode\u003edynamic_cast\u003c/code\u003e will return \u003ccode\u003enullptr\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003ePros of dynamic type checking\u003c/strong\u003e:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eIncreased flexibility\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eOften easier to implement generics that operate on many different types of data\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eSimpler code due to fewer type annotations\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eMakes for faster prototyping\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eCons of dynamic type checking\u003c/strong\u003e:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eWe detect errors much later\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eCode is slower due to run time type checking\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eRequires more testing for the same level of assurance\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eNo way to guarantee safety across all possible executions (unlike static type checking)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch4 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eAddendum: Dynamic Type Checking in Statically-Typed Languages\u003c/h4\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-addendum-dynamic-type-checking-in-statically-typed-languages\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Addendum: Dynamic Type Checking in Statically-Typed Languages\" languages:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ewhen downcasting (in C++)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ewhen disambiguating variants (think Haskell!)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e(depending on the implementation) potentially in runtime generics\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch4 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eDuck Typing\u003c/h4\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-duck-typing\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Duck Typing\" href=\"#duck-typing\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDuck typing emerges as a consequence of dynamic typing. With static typing, we determine the what operations work on a particular value/variable based on the type of the value/variable. But a consequence of dynamic typing is that variables no longer have a fixed type. This means that we can pass a value of any type to a function, and as long as the type of the value implements all of the operations used in the function, the code should work fine.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eConsider the following example:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"# Python \u0026quot;duck\u0026quot; typing\nclass Duck:\n def swim(self):\n  print(\u0026quot;Paddle paddle paddle\u0026quot;)\n\nclass When it gets to \u003ccode\u003eProfessor\u003c/code\u003e, which doesn't implement \u003ccode\u003eswim\u003c/code\u003e, that's when you get the error.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe values you pass to \u003ccode\u003eprocess\u003c/code\u003e only need to implement \u003ccode\u003eswim\u003c/code\u003e, they do not have to be related to each other. Duck typing has some interesting applications.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch4 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eSupporting upper):\n    self.upper = upper\n    self.n = lower\n  def __iter__(self):\n    return self\n  def __next__(self):\n    if self.n \u0026lt; self.upper:\n      s = self.n ** 3\n      self.n += 1\n      return s\n    else:\n      raise StopIteration\n\nfor i in Cubes(1, 4):\n  print(i)             # prints 1, 8, 27\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e# Python duck typing for class=\"pl-en\"\u003eprint\u003c/span\u003e(\u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\"Same!\"\u003c/span\u003e)\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eOther dynamically typed languages also stroke!\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e{: .note }\nIt is possible to have something similar to duck typing in statically typed languages (like C++) as well. In C++, this is done using templates; there's also runtime generics in Java, Rust's generics system, etc.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eGradual Typing\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-gradual-typing\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Gradual Typing\" href=\"#gradual-typing\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eGradual typing is a hybrid approach between static and dynamic typing. It's used by a few well known languages like PHP and TypeScript, so it merits discussion.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIn gradual typing, some variables may have explicitly annotated types, while others may not. This allows the type checker to partially verify type safety prior to execution, and perform the rest of the checks during run time.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWith gradual typing, you can choose whether to specify a type for variables/parameters. If a variable is untyped, then type errors for that variable are detected at run time. But if a variable is typed, then it's possible to detect some type errors at compile time. But what if we pass an untyped variable as an argument to a typed variable? Look at the following code snipped for a concrete example.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"def square(x: int):\n  return x * x\n\ndef what_happens(y):\n  print(square(y))\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003edef\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003esquare\u003c/span\u003e(\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003ex\u003c/span\u003e: \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003eint\u003c/span\u003e):\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003ereturn\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003ex\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e*\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003ex\u003c/span\u003e\n\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003edef\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003ewhat_happens\u003c/span\u003e(\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003ey\u003c/span\u003e):\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003eprint\u003c/span\u003e(\u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003esquare\u003c/span\u003e(\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003ey\u003c/span\u003e))\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThis is actually allowed in gradually typed languages! If you pass an untyped variable as an argument to \u003ccode\u003ewhat_happens\u003c/code\u003e, the type checker will check for errors during run time. This way, if you do use an invalid type, the program will generate an error the moment an incompatible type is detected.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eLet's try and classify a language.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-kotlin notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"fun greet(name: String) {\n  print(\u0026quot;Hello, $name!\u0026quot;)\n}\n\nfun main() {\n  var n = \u0026quot;Graciela\u0026quot;;\n  greet(n);\n\n  n = 10;\n}\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003efun\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003egreet\u003c/span\u003e(\u003cspan class=\"pl-smi\"\u003ename\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003eString\u003c/span\u003e) {\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003eprint\u003c/span\u003e(\u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003eHello, \u003cspan class=\"pl-e\"\u003e$name\u003c/span\u003e!\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/span\u003e)\n}\n\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003efun\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-en\"\u003emain\u003c/span\u003e() {\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003evar\u003c/span\u003e n \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003eGraciela\u003cspan class=\"pl-pds\"\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/span\u003e;\n  greet(n);\n\n  n \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e10\u003c/span\u003e;\n}\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIs this language dynamically, statically or gradually typed, given that the code generates the following error?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-text-shell-session notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"The integer literal does not conform to the expected type String\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003eThe integer literal does not conform to the expected type String\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eAnswer\u003c/strong\u003e: Even though it doesn't look like it at first glance, the language is statically typed, since you can't assign \u003ccode\u003en\u003c/code\u003e to a value of a new type. This means that \u003ccode\u003en\u003c/code\u003e has a fixed type, and that the language is using type inference. This language is actually Kotlin!\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eStrong typing\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-strong-typing\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Strong typing\" href=\"#strong-typing\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eNow that we have a good idea of static and dynamic typing, we're going to look at the various type checking approaches on the basis of strictness. A strongly typed language ensures that we will \u003cstrong\u003enever\u003c/strong\u003e have \u003cem\u003eundefined behaviour\u003c/em\u003e at run time due to type issues. This means that in a strongly typed language, there is no possibility of an unchecked run time type error.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e{: .note }\nThe definition of strong typing is disputed. Many academics argue for a stronger definition (e.g. all conversions between types should be explicit, the language should have explicit type annotations for all variables, etc.). But ultimately while these definitions may make a languages type system stricter, they don't impact the languages type or memory safety.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThese are the minimum requirements for a language to be strongly typed:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003ethe language is type-safe\u003c/strong\u003e: the language will prevent an operation on a variable \u003ccode\u003ex\u003c/code\u003e if \u003ccode\u003ex\u003c/code\u003es type doesn't support that operation.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"int x;\nDog d;\na = 5 * d; // Prevented\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eint\u003c/span\u003e x;\nDog d;\na = \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e5\u003c/span\u003e * d; \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e Prevented\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003ethe language is memory safe\u003c/strong\u003e: the language prevents inappropriate memory accesses (e.g., out-of-bounds array accesses, accessing a dangling pointer)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"int arr[5], *ptr;\ncout \u0026lt;\u0026lt; arr[10]; // Prevented\ncout \u0026lt;\u0026lt; *ptr; // Prevented\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eint\u003c/span\u003e arr[\u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e5\u003c/span\u003e], *ptr;\ncout \u0026lt;\u0026lt; arr[\u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e10\u003c/span\u003e]; \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e Prevented\u003c/span\u003e\ncout \u0026lt;\u0026lt; *ptr; \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e Prevented\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThese can be enforced either statically or dynamically!\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eLanguages usually use a few techniques to implement strong typing:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ebefore an expression is evaluated, the compiler/interpreter validates that all of the operands used in the expression have compatible types.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eall conversions between different types are checked and if the types are incompatible (e.g., converting an int to a Dog), then an exception will be generated.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003epointers are either set to null or assigned to point at a valid object at creation.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eaccesses to arrays are bounds checked; pointer arithmetic is bounds-checked.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003ethe language ensures objects can't be used after they are destroyed.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIn general, strongly typed languages prevent operations on incompatible types or invalid memory.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhy do we need memory safety?\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-why-do-we-need-memory-safety\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Why do we need memory safety?\" href=\"#why-do-we-need-memory-safety\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhy do strongly typed langauges require memory safety? To answer this question, consider the following example in C++ (a weakly typed language).\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"// C++\nint arr[3] = {10, 20, 30};\nfloat salary = 120000.50;\n\ncout \u0026lt;\u0026lt; arr[3]; // out-of-bounds access\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e C++\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eint\u003c/span\u003e arr[\u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e3\u003c/span\u003e] = {\u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e10\u003c/span\u003e, \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e20\u003c/span\u003e, \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e30\u003c/span\u003e};\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003efloat\u003c/span\u003e salary = \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e120000.50\u003c/span\u003e;\n\ncout \u0026lt;\u0026lt; arr[\u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e3\u003c/span\u003e]; \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e out-of-bounds access\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003earr[3]\u003c/code\u003e actually access the value stored in \u003ccode\u003esalary\u003c/code\u003e, since all local variables are stored on the stack. So if a language is not memory safe, then it's possible to access a value (like \u003ccode\u003esalary\u003c/code\u003e) using an invalid type (\u003ccode\u003eint\u003c/code\u003e instead of \u003ccode\u003efloat\u003c/code\u003e). Accessing a dangling pointer is another example of how memory safety can violate type safety.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cmarkdown-accessiblity-table\u003e\u003ctable\u003e\n\u003cthead\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003cth align=\"center\"\u003e\u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"/UCLA-CS-131/fall-23-website/blob/main/lectures/%7B%7Bsite.baseurl%7D%7D/assets/lecture-notes/07/ram-image-weak-safety.png\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"/UCLA-CS-131/fall-23-website/raw/main/lectures/%7B%7Bsite.baseurl%7D%7D/assets/lecture-notes/07/ram-image-weak-safety.png\" alt=\"cpp-weak-type\" style=\"max-width: 100%;\"\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/th\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003c/thead\u003e\n\u003ctbody\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd align=\"center\"\u003eIn C++, \u003ccode\u003earr[3]\u003c/code\u003e would actually access the value stored in \u003ccode\u003esalary\u003c/code\u003e as if it were an integer!\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003c/tbody\u003e\n\u003c/table\u003e\u003c/markdown-accessiblity-table\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"// Accessing a dangling pointer\nfloat *ptr = new float[100];\ndelete [] ptr;\ncout \u0026lt;\u0026lt; *ptr; // is this still a float?\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e//\u003c/span\u003e Accessing a dangling pointer\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003efloat\u003c/span\u003e *ptr = \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003enew\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003efloat\u003c/span\u003e[\u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e100\u003c/span\u003e];\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003edelete []\u003c/span\u003e ptr;\ncout \u0026lt;\u0026lt; Let's look at a concrete example in Java, a strongly typed language.\nConsider the following snippet of code.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-java notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"public void petAnimal(Animal a) {\n  a.pet(); This is \u003cem\u003eundefined behaviour\u003c/em\u003e (we will cover undefined behaviour later in this lecture).\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhy should we prefer strongly typed languages? overflows).\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eThey allow for early detection and fixing of -->main</span></div></div></span><span data-component="trailingVisual" class="Box-sc-g0xbh4-0 hzSPyu"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" role="img" class="octicon octicon-triangle-down" .354 0l3.396-3.396A.25.25 0 0 0 11.396 7H4.604a.25.25 0 0 0-.177.427Z"></path></svg></span></span></button><button hidden="" data-hotkey-scope="read-only-cursor-text-area"></button></div><div <p dir="auto">{: .note }
Matt here! After hearing from Brian Kernighan (which was awesome!), we covered slides 16-52 of <a href="https://docs.google.com/presentation/d/196AgYxc9mFypCwZwHAMNtbylKsfsANX8/edit?usp=sharing&amp;ouid=101757866260235503028&amp;rtpof=true&amp;sd=true" rel="nofollow">Data Palooza</a>.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Table of Contents</h2><a id="user-content-table-of-contents" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Table of Contents" href="#table-of-contents"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
